{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01KoTtNhdzzDG7yWEe1TauNK","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: #pragma once\\n2: \\n3: #include <fcntl.h>\\n4: #include <sys/stat.h>\\n5: #include <sys/un.h>\\n6: #include <unistd.h>\\n7: \\n8: #include <array>\\n9: #include <atomic>\\n10: #include <cstdint>\\n11: #include <string>\\n12: \\n13: #include \\\"envoy/common/platform.h\\\"\\n14: #include \\\"envoy/server/hot_restart.h\\\"\\n15: #include \\\"envoy/server/options.h\\\"\\n16: #include \\\"envoy/stats/scope.h\\\"\\n17: \\n18: #include \\\"source/common/common/assert.h\\\"\\n19: #include \\\"source/server/hot_restart.pb.h\\\"\\n20: \\n21: namespace Envoy {\\n22: namespace Server {\\n23: \\n24: class RpcStream : public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::main> {\\n25: public:\\n26:   enum class Blocking { Yes, No };\\n27: \\n28:   explicit RpcStream(uint64_t base_id) : base_id_(base_id) {}\\n29:   ~RpcStream();\\n30:   void initDomainSocketAddress(sockaddr_un* address);\\n31:   sockaddr_un createDomainSocketAddress(uint64_t id, const std::string& role,\\n32:                                         const std::string& socket_path, mode_t socket_mode);\\n33:   void bindDomainSocket(uint64_t id, const std::string& role, const std::string& socket_path,\\n34:                         mode_t socket_mode);\\n35: \\n36:   // Protocol description:\\n37:   //\\n38:   // In each direction between parent<-->child, a series of pairs of:\\n39:   //   A uint64 'length' (bytes in network order),\\n40:   //   followed by 'length' bytes of a serialized HotRestartMessage.\\n41:   // Each new message must start in a new sendmsg datagram, i.e. 'length' must always start at\\n42:   // byte 0. Each sendmsg datagram can be up to 4096 bytes (including 'length' if present). When\\n43:   // the serialized protobuf is longer than 4096-8 bytes, and so cannot fit in just one datagram,\\n44:   // it is delivered by a series of datagrams. In each of these continuation datagrams, the\\n45:   // protobuf data starts at byte 0.\\n46:   //\\n47:   // There is no mechanism to explicitly pair responses to requests. However, the child initiates\\n48:   // all exchanges, and blocks until a reply is received, so there is implicit pairing.\\n49:   bool sendHotRestartMessage(sockaddr_un& address, const envoy::HotRestartMessage& proto,\\n50:                              bool allow_failure = false);\\n51: \\n52:   // Receive data, possibly enough to build one of our protocol messages.\\n53:   // If block is true, blocks until a full protocol message is available.\\n54:   // If block is false, returns nullptr if we run out of data to receive before a full protocol\\n55:   // message is available. In either case, the HotRestartingBase may end up buffering some data\\n56:   // for the next protocol message, even if the function returns a protobuf.\\n57:   std::unique_ptr<envoy::HotRestartMessage> receiveHotRestartMessage(Blocking block);\\n58:   bool replyIsExpectedType(const envoy::HotRestartMessage* proto,\\n59:                            envoy::HotRestartMessage::Reply::ReplyCase oneof_type) const;\\n60: \\n61:   int domain_socket_{-1};\\n62: \\n63: private:\\n64:   void getPassedFdIfPresent(envoy::HotRestartMessage* out, msghdr* message);\\n65:   std::unique_ptr<envoy::HotRestartMessage> parseProtoAndResetState();\\n66:   void initRecvBufIfNewMessage();\\n67:   // An int in [0, MaxConcurrentProcesses). As hot restarts happen, each next process gets the\\n68:   // next of 0,1,2,0,1,...\\n69:   // A HotRestartingBase's domain socket's name contains its base_id_ value, and so we can use\\n70:   // this value to determine which domain socket name to treat as our parent, and which to treat\\n71:   // as our child. (E.g. if we are 2, 1 is parent and 0 is child).\\n72:   const uint64_t base_id_;\\n73:   // State for the receiving half of the protocol.\\n74:   //\\n75:   // When filled, the size in bytes that the in-flight HotRestartMessage should be.\\n76:   // When empty, we're ready to start receiving a new message (starting with a uint64 'length').\\n77:   absl::optional<uint64_t> expected_proto_length_;\\n78:   // How much of the current in-flight message (including both the uint64 'length', plus the proto\\n79:   // itself) we have received. Once this equals expected_proto_length_ + sizeof(uint64_t), we're\\n80:   // ready to parse the HotRestartMessage. Should be set to 0 in between messages, to indicate\\n81:   // readiness for a new message.\\n82:   uint64_t cur_msg_recvd_bytes_{};\\n83:   // The first 8 bytes will always be the raw net-order bytes of the current value of\\n84:   // expected_proto_length_. The protobuf partial data starts at byte 8.\\n85:   // Should be resized to 0 in between messages, to indicate readiness for a new message.\\n86:   std::vector<uint8_t> recv_buf_;\\n87: };\\n88: \\n89: /**\\n90:  * Logic shared by the implementations of both sides of the child<-->parent hot restart protocol:\\n91:  * domain socket communication, and our ad hoc RPC protocol.\\n92:  */\\n93: class HotRestartingBase : public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::main> {\\n94: protected:\\n95:   HotRestartingBase(uint64_t base_id)\\n96:       : main_rpc_stream_(base_id), udp_forwarding_rpc_stream_(base_id) {}\\n97: \\n98:   // Returns a Gauge that tracks hot-restart generation, where every successive\\n99:   // child increments this number.\\n100:   static Stats::Gauge& hotRestartGeneration(Stats::Scope& scope);\\n101: \\n102:   // A stream over a unix socket between the parent and child instances, used\\n103:   // for the child instance to request socket information and control draining\\n104:   // and shutdown of the parent.\\n105:   RpcStream main_rpc_stream_;\\n106: \\n107:   // A separate channel is used for udp forwarding because udp forwarding can\\n108:   // begin while communication on the main channel is still occurring. The hot\\n109:   // restarter is single-threaded, so we don't have to worry about packets coming\\n110:   // in a jumbled order, but there are two instances of the hot restarter, the\\n111:   // parent and the child; it is possible for the child to send a udp packet\\n112:   // while the parent is sending a request on the main channel, for which it will\\n113:   // expect to receive a response (and not an unrelated udp packet). The implementation spans multiple C++ source files in github.com/envoyproxy/envoy:\\n\\n## Core Interface and Implementation\\n\\n**envoy/server/hot_restart.h** defines the abstract `HotRestart` interface with methods for draining parent listeners, duplicating parent listen sockets, registering UDP forwarding listeners, and merging parent stats.\\n\\n**source/server/hot_restart_impl.h** and **source/server/hot_restart_impl.cc** provide the main Linux implementation of hot restart. The `HotRestartImpl` class contains two internal instances (`as_child_` and `as_parent_`) to handle both parent and child roles. It also manages a `SharedMemory` structure used for inter-process coordination that includes version information, flags (like `SHMEM_FLAGS_INITIALIZING`), and process-shared pthread mutexes for logging synchronization.\\n\\n**source/server/hot_restart_nop_impl.h** provides a no-operation implementation used when hot restart is disabled.\\n\\n## Protocol Definition\\n\\n**source/server/hot_restart.proto** defines the `HotRestartMessage` protocol with request and reply message types. Requests include: `PassListenSocket` (to get a listening socket from parent), `ShutdownAdmin`, `Stats` (to request parent stats), `DrainListeners`, `Terminate`, `ForwardedUdpPacket` (for QUIC packet forwarding), and `TestConnection` (for connection testing). Replies include socket file descriptors, admin shutdown response with original start time, and aggregated statistics with counters, gauges, and dynamic stat metadata.\\n\\n## RPC Protocol and Socket Communication\\n\\n**source/server/hot_restarting_base.h** and **source/server/hot_restarting_base.cc** implement the core `RpcStream` class that handles the domain socket communication protocol. The protocol uses Unix domain sockets in datagram mode (`SOCK_DGRAM`) with a custom serialization format: a 64-bit network-byte-order length field followed by a protobuf message payload. Messages can span multiple datagrams up to 4096 bytes each. The `RpcStream` class implements `sendHotRestartMessage()` which serializes protobuf messages and sends them via `sendmsg()` with support for file descriptor passing via `SCM_RIGHTS` control data. The `receiveHotRestartMessage()` method uses `recvmsg()` to receive messages with optional blocking, buffering partial messages across multiple `recvmsg()` calls, and extracting passed file descriptors via `getPassedFdIfPresent()`. The base class `HotRestartingBase` maintains two `RpcStream` instances: `main_rpc_stream_` for main communication and `udp_forwarding_rpc_stream_` for UDP packet forwarding to avoid interference.\\n\\n## Child Process Implementation\\n\\n**source/server/hot_restarting_child.h** and **source/server/hot_restarting_child.cc** implement `HotRestartingChild` which handles the child process side of hot restart. The child is responsible for:\\n\\n- **Parent Connection**: Stores parent addresses computed from the restart epoch number\\n- **Socket Duplication**: Implements `duplicateParentListenSocket()` by sending a `PassListenSocket` request to the parent and extracting the returned file descriptor\\n- **Drain Signaling**: Implements `drainParentListeners()` by sending a `DrainListeners` request to notify the parent that the child is ready\\n- **Stats Merging**: Implements `getParentStats()` to request stats from the parent and `mergeParentStats()` to incorporate parent stats into the child's stats store\\n- **UDP Forwarding Context**: The `UdpForwardingContext` class maintains a map of registered UDP listeners to support QUIC packet forwarding from parent to child\\n- **Parent Drained Callbacks**: Implements `Network::ParentDrainedCallbackRegistrar` to allow listeners to register callbacks that fire when the parent finishes draining\\n- **Initialization**: The `initialize()` method sets up the `socket_event_udp_forwarding_` file event to handle incoming UDP packets from the parent\\n\\n## Parent Process Implementation\\n\\n**source/server/hot_restarting_parent.h** and **source/server/hot_restarting_parent.cc** implement `HotRestartingParent` and its nested `Internal` class. The parent process:\\n\\n- **Listens for Requests**: The `onSocketEvent()` method receives requests from the child and dispatches them\\n- **Socket Passing**: `getListenSocketsForChild()` locates the listening socket matching the child's request and passes the file descriptor back via `sendHotRestartMessage()` with fd control data\\n- **Admin Shutdown**: `shutdownAdmin()` shuts down admin processing and returns the original start time and reuse_port default setting\\n- **Stats Export**: `exportStatsToChild()` iterates over all sinks gauges and counters, latches counter values, and exports them along with dynamic stat metadata\\n- **Listener Draining**: `drainListeners()` initiates the drain sequence for all listeners\\n- **UDP Packet Forwarding**: The `handle()` method receives UDP packets and forwards them to the child via the UDP forwarding channel\\n\\n## Shared Memory and Synchronization\\n\\n**source/server/hot_restart_impl.h** defines the `SharedMemory` structure with `size_`, `version_`, and process-shared pthread mutexes for `log_lock_` and `access_log_lock_`. The `attachSharedMemory()` function in **source/server/hot_restart_impl.cc** manages the lifecycle of this shared memory segment using POSIX `shm_open()`, `mmap()`, and synchronization flags.\\n\\n## OS Abstraction\\n\\n**envoy/api/os_sys_calls_hot_restart.h** defines the abstract `HotRestartOsSysCalls` interface for shared memory operations (`shmOpen()`, `shmUnlink()`). **source/common/api/posix/os_sys_calls_impl_hot_restart.h** provides the POSIX implementation via `HotRestartOsSysCallsImpl`.\\n\\n## Key Mechanisms\\n\\n1. **Parent/Child Process Handshake**: Established via Unix domain socket addresses computed from the restart epoch number, allowing processes to discover each other\\n2. **File Descriptor Passing**: Used in `PassListenSocket` replies to transfer listening sockets from parent to child via `SCM_RIGHTS` control data in `recvmsg()`/`sendmsg()`\\n3. **Drain Sequence**: Initiated when child sends `DrainListeners`, triggering parent listeners to drain existing connections while child takes over new ones\\n4. **Child Readiness Signaling**: Child calls `drainParentListeners()` to signal that it has initialized, clearing the `SHMEM_FLAGS_INITIALIZING` flag so another new child can start\\n5. **Stats Merging**: Parent exports gauge values and counter deltas with dynamic stat name metadata so child can maintain continuity of metrics\\n6. **UDP Forwarding for QUIC**: Separate UDP forwarding RPC channel allows the parent to forward packets for connections the child should handle during draining\\n7. **Shared Memory Coordination**: The `SharedMemory` structure with atomic flags and process-shared mutexes synchronizes between parent and child processes\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":6,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2167,"cache_read_input_tokens":89570,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2167},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"ab22946d-3a6b-4350-916b-d8733fb55e82","uuid":"1764b18c-17df-411f-8a68-667559a65b5f"}
